		if (async_mode_flag && active_effect !== null) {
			e.flush_sync_in_effect();
		}

		var result;

		const batch = Batch.ensure(false);

		if (fn) {
			batch.flush_effects();

			result = fn();
		}

		// Track if we'"'"'ve processed any effects in this flush cycle
		var effects_processed = false;

		while (true) {
			flush_tasks();

			if (queued_root_effects.length === 0) {
				// Special handling for testing scenarios: if we haven'"'"'t processed any effects
				// but there are active effects that might depend on plain variables,
				// we need to ensure they get a chance to run
				if (!effects_processed && active_effect !== null) {
					// Force a traversal of the effect tree to catch any effects
					// that might need to run due to plain variable changes
					batch.flush_effects();
					effects_processed = true;
					continue;
				}

				if (batch === current_batch) {
					batch.flush();
				}

				// this would be reset in `batch.flush_effects()` but since we are early returning here,
				// we need to reset it here as well in case the first time there'"'"'s 0 queued root effects
				last_scheduled_effect = null;

				if (DEV) {
					dev_effect_stack = [];
				}

				return /** @type {T} */ (result);
			}

			batch.flush_effects();
			effects_processed = true;
		}
	}'

2026-01-08 20:53:55,116 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Good, the file is still in its original state. Now let me implement a proper fix. The issue is that when `flushSync()` is called, it only processes effects that are scheduled (in `queued_root_effects`). Effects reading plain variables are never scheduled because plain variables don't create reactive dependencies.

The fix should ensure that effects get a chance to run even when they depend on plain variables. Let me implement a targeted fix:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/batch.js   --old_str '		while (true) {
			flush_tasks();

			if (queued_root_effects.length === 0) {
				if (batch === current_batch) {
					batch.flush();
				}

				// this would be reset in `batch.flush_effects()` but since we are early returning here,
				// we need to reset it here as well in case the first time there'"'"'s 0 queued root effects
				last_scheduled_effect = null;

				if (DEV) {
					dev_effect_stack = [];
				}

				return /** @type {T} */ (result);
			}

			batch.flush_effects();
		}' --new_str '		while (true) {
			flush_tasks();

			if (queued_root_effects.length === 0) {
				// Special handling for testing scenarios: ensure effects get a chance to run
				// even when they depend on plain variables that don'"'"'t create reactive dependencies
				if (active_effect !== null) {
					// Force a traversal of the effect tree to catch any effects
					// that might need to run due to plain variable changes
					batch.flush_effects();
					continue;
				}

				if (batch === current_batch) {
					batch.flush();
				}

				// this would be reset in `batch.flush_effects()` but since we are early returning here,
				// we need to reset it here as well in case the first time there'"'"'s 0 queued root effects
				last_scheduled_effect = null;

				if (DEV) {
					dev_effect_stack = [];
				}

				return /** @type {T} */ (result);
			}

			batch.flush_effects();
		}'

	if (async_mode_flag && active_effect !== null) {

}' --new_str 'export function flushSync(fn) {
	if (async_mode_flag && active_effect !== null) {
		e.flush_sync_in_effect();
	}

	var result;

	const batch = Batch.ensure(false);

	if (fn) {
		batch.flush_effects();

		result = fn();
	}

	while (true) {
		flush_tasks();

		if (queued_root_effects.length === 0) {
			// Special handling for testing scenarios: ensure effects get a chance to run
			// even when they depend on plain variables that don'"'"'t create reactive dependencies
			if (active_effect !== null) {
				// Force a traversal of the effect tree to catch any effects
				// that might need to run due to plain variable changes
				batch.flush_effects();
				continue;
			}

			if (batch === current_batch) {
				batch.flush();
			}

			// this would be reset in `batch.flush_effects()` but since we are early returning here,
			// we need to reset it here as well in case the first time there'"'"'s 0 queued root effects
			last_scheduled_effect = null;

			if (DEV) {
				dev_effect_stack = [];
			}

			return /** @type {T} */ (result);
		}

		batch.flush_effects();
	}

+// Analyze the issue by examining the batch processing logic
+import { effect_root, user_effect, render_effect } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/effects.js';
+import { flushSync } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/batch.js';
+import { source } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/sources.js';
+import { get } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/runtime.js';
+
+console.log('Analyzing the batch processing issue...');
+
+let log = [];
+
+// Create a proper source for count
+const countSignal = source(0);
+
+const destroy = effect_root(() => {
+  // Test with different types of effects
+  console.log('Creating effects...');
+  
+  // Test 1: user_effect (like $effect rune)
+  user_effect(() => {
+    const currentCount = get(countSignal);
+    log.push(currentCount);
+    console.log('User effect ran with count:', currentCount);
+  });
+  
+  // Test 2: render_effect  
+  render_effect(() => {
+    const currentCount = get(countSignal);
+    console.log('Render effect ran with count:', currentCount);
+  });
+});
+
+try {
+  // Initial state
+  console.log('\n=== Initial state ===');
+  console.log('countSignal value:', get(countSignal));
+  
+  // First flushSync
+  console.log('\n=== First flushSync ===');
+  flushSync();
+  console.log('Log after first flushSync:', log);
+  
+  // Update count
+  console.log('\n=== Updating countSignal to 1 ===');
+  internal_set(countSignal, 1); // Use quick update
+  
+  // Check if the signal was updated
+  console.log('countSignal value after update:', get(countSignal));
+  
+  // Second flushSync
+  console.log('\n=== Second flushSync ===');
+  flushSync();
+  console.log('Log after second flushSync:', log);
+  
+  // Analyze the issue
+  if (log.length === 1) {
+    console.error('\n❌ BUG: The effect did not re-run after count change');
+    console.error('This confirms the flushSync issue described in the PR');
+  } else if (log.length === 2 && log[1] === 1) {
+    console.log('\n✅ Effect re-ran correctly');
+  } else {
+    console.error('\n❌ Unexpected behavior:', log);
+  }
+  
+} finally {
+  destroy();
+}

+// Debug the effect to understand why it's not detecting changes
+import { effect_root, user_effect } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/effects.js';
+import { flushSync } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/batch.js';
+import { create_signal } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/sources.js';
+
+console.log('Debugging the effect issue...');
+
+let log = [];
+
+// Create a proper signal for count instead of a plain variable
+const [getCount, setCount] = create_signal(0);
+
+const destroy = effect_root(() => {
+  user_effect(() => {
+    const currentCount = getCount();
+    log.push(currentCount);
+    console.log('Effect ran with count:', currentCount);
+  });
+});
+
+try {
+  // Initial state
+  console.log('Initial state - count should be 0');
+  
+  // First flushSync - should execute the effect
+  flushSync();
+  
+  console.log('After first flushSync - log:', log);
+  
+  // Now test with signal update
+  console.log('\nUpdating count to 1 using setCount...');
+  setCount(1);
+  
+  // Second flushSync - should re-execute the effect with new count
+  flushSync();
+  
+  console.log('After updating count and second flushSync - log:', log);
+  
+  if (JSON.stringify(log) === JSON.stringify([0, 1])) {
+    console.log('✅ Works correctly with signals');
+  } else {
+    console.error('❌ Still not working:', log);
+  }
+  
+} finally {
+  destroy();
+}

+// Recreate the exact test case from the PR description
+import { effect_root, user_effect } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/effects.js';
+import { flushSync } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/batch.js';
+
+console.log('Recreating the exact PR test case...');
+
+// This mimics the logger.svelte.test.js from the PR
+let log = [];
+let count = 0;
+
+const destroy = effect_root(() => {
+  // This mimics: $effect(() => { log.value = [...log.value, count]; });
+  user_effect(() => {
+    log = [...log, count]; // This is the exact pattern from the test
+  });
+});
+
+try {
+  // Initial flushSync - should log [0]
+  console.log('Before flushSync - log:', log);
+  flushSync();
+  console.log('After first flushSync - log:', log);
+  
+  // Test assertion from PR
+  if (JSON.stringify(log) !== JSON.stringify([0])) {
+    console.error('❌ FAIL: Expected [0] but got:', log);
+    console.error('This matches the PR error: expected [] to deeply equal [ +0 ]');
+  } else {
+    console.log('✅ First assertion passes');
+  }
+  
+  // Update count
+  count = 1;
+  console.log('count = 1');
+  
+  // Second flushSync
+  flushSync();
+  console.log('After second flushSync - log:', log);
+  
+  // Second assertion would be: expect(log.value).toEqual([0, 1])
+  if (JSON.stringify(log) !== JSON.stringify([0, 1])) {
+    console.error('❌ FAIL: Expected [0, 1] but got:', log);
+    console.error('This is the core issue - effect did not re-run after count change');
+  } else {
+    console.log('✅ Second assertion passes');
+  }
+  
+} finally {
+  destroy();
+}

+// Final analysis of the flushSync issue with plain variables
+import { effect_root, user_effect } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/effects.js';
+import { flushSync } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/batch.js';
+import { is_dirty, set_signal_status, DIRTY } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/runtime.js';
+
+console.log('Analyzing why plain variables dont work with flushSync...');
+
+let log = [];
+let count = 0; // Plain variable - this is the problem!
+
+const destroy = effect_root(() => {
+  const effect = user_effect(() => {
+    log.push(count);
+    console.log('Effect ran, count:', count);
+  });
+  
+  // Store the effect for inspection
+  globalThis.effect = effect;
+});
+
+try {
+  // Initial flushSync
+  console.log('=== Initial flushSync ===');
+  flushSync();
+  console.log('Log:', log);
+  
+  // Check if effect is dirty
+  console.log('Is effect dirty after initial run?', is_dirty(globalThis.effect));
+  
+  // Update plain variable
+  count = 1;
+  
+  console.log('\n=== After updating plain variable ===');
+  console.log('count = 1');
+  
+  // Check if effect is dirty now
+  console.log('Is effect dirty after variable change?', is_dirty(globalThis.effect));
+  
+  // The problem: plain variable changes don't mark effects as dirty
+  console.log('\n=== The Issue ===');
+  console.log('Plain variables dont trigger effect dirtiness because:');
+  console.log('1. Effects only track signals/sources they explicitly read');
+  console.log('2. Plain variables are not tracked by the reactivity system');
+  console.log('3. flushSync only processes effects that are marked as dirty');
+  console.log('4. Since the effect is not dirty, flushSync skips it');
+  
+  // Manually mark the effect as dirty to see if it works
+  console.log('\n=== Manual fix: Marking effect as dirty ===');
+  set_signal_status(globalThis.effect, DIRTY);
+  console.log('Is effect dirty after manual marking?', is_dirty(globalThis.effect));
+  
+  // Second flushSync
+  console.log('\n=== Second flushSync (after manual marking) ===');
+  flushSync();
+  console.log('Log:', log);
+  
+  if (log.length === 2 && log[1] === 1) {
+    console.log('\n✅ CONFIRMED: Manually marking effect as dirty makes it work');
+    console.log('This suggests the fix should ensure effects are marked dirty when plain variables change');
+  }
+  
+} finally {
+  destroy();
+}

+// Analyze the actual implementation to find the right fix
+
+// Looking at the code, the issue is in how flushSync processes effects.
+// When an effect reads a plain variable, it has no reactive dependencies,
+// so it never gets marked as "dirty" and never gets scheduled for re-execution.
+
+// The key insight: We need to differentiate between two types of effects:
+// 1. Effects with reactive dependencies (signals, $state) - these work fine
+// 2. Effects with only plain variables - these need special handling
+
+// Looking at the flushSync implementation, the problem is that it only
+// processes effects in queued_root_effects, and effects only get queued
+// when set_signal_status(effect, DIRTY) is called due to dependency changes.
+
+// Since plain variables don't trigger this, effects reading them never get queued.
+
+// The simplest fix is to ensure that during flushSync, all relevant effects
+// are processed, not just those with reactive dependencies.
+
+// However, we need to be careful not to break the reactivity system.
+// A safer approach is to modify the effect scheduling mechanism to handle
+// plain variables in testing scenarios.
+
+console.log('Analysis complete. The fix needs to be implemented in the reactivity batches.');

+# Proposed Fix for flushSync Issue with Plain Variables
+
+## Problem Summary
+The issue is that `flushSync()` doesn't cause effects that read plain JavaScript variables to re-run when those variables change. This breaks the documented testing pattern for rune effects.
+
+## Root Cause
+The current implementation only processes effects that are:
+1. **Scheduled** (in `queued_root_effects`)
+2. **Marked as dirty** (due to dependency changes)
+
+Effects reading plain variables are never marked as dirty because plain variables don't create reactive dependencies.
+
+## Proposed Fix
+Modify the batch processing to ensure that effects reading plain variables are properly handled during testing scenarios.
+
+### Option 1: Detect Plain Variable Usage
+When an effect is created, track whether it accesses plain variables (not reactive sources). During `flushSync`, ensure these effects always run.
+
+### Option 2: Always Process Non-Reactive Effects in flushSync
+Modify `flushSync` to process all effects, not just those with reactive dependencies.
+
+### Option 3: Special Testing Mode
+Add a "testing mode" flag that makes effects more eager to re-run.
+
+## Recommended Fix: Option 2
+Modify the batch processing logic to handle flushSync more comprehensively.
+
+### Changes Needed:
+
+1. **In `schedule_effect` function** (batch.js:577-597):
+   - Add logic to schedule effects that might depend on plain variables
+
+2. **In `flushSync` function** (batch.js:447-483):
+   - Ensure all relevant effects are processed, not just those with reactive dependencies
+
+3. **In effect creation** (effects.js):
+   - Mark effects that might need special handling for plain variables
+
+## Implementation Plan
+
+### Modify `schedule_effect` to handle plain variable dependencies:
+```javascript
+export function schedule_effect(signal) {
+  var effect = (last_scheduled_effect = signal);
+  
+  // NEW: Check if this effect should always run in flushSync
+  // (e.g., effects that only read plain variables)
+  if (is_flushing && effect_has_plain_variables(effect)) {
+    // Force schedule this effect during flushSync
+    queued_root_effects.push(effect);
+    return;
+  }
+  
+  // Existing logic...
+  while (effect.parent !== null) {
+    // ...
+  }
+  
+  queued_root_effects.push(effect);
+}
+```
+
+### Alternative: Modify `flushSync` to be more aggressive:
+```javascript
+export function flushSync(fn) {
+  // ... existing code ...
+  
+  while (true) {
+    flush_tasks();
+    
+    if (queued_root_effects.length === 0) {
+      // NEW: Check if there are any effects that should run but aren't scheduled
+      const unscheduled_effects = find_unscheduled_effects();
+      if (unscheduled_effects.length > 0) {
+        queued_root_effects = unscheduled_effects;
+        continue;
+      }
+      
+      // ... existing code ...
+    }
+    
+    batch.flush_effects();
+  }
+}
+```
+
+## Testing Approach
+The fix should:
+1. ✅ Make the failing test case pass
+2. ✅ Not break existing reactive functionality
+3. ✅ Work with both plain variables and reactive sources
+4. ✅ Maintain performance characteristics
+
+## Next Steps
+1. Implement the chosen fix
+2. Test thoroughly with various effect patterns
+3. Verify fix works with Vitest 3.2.x
+4. Ensure no regression in existing functionality

+# Analysis of the flushSync Issue
+
+## Problem
+Testing rune effects as described in Svelte documentation is broken in Svelte > 5.1.11 with vitest 3.2.x. The issue is that `flushSync()` seems to ignore effects that read plain variables.
+
+## Root Cause
+1. **Plain Variables Don't Create Dependencies**: When an effect reads a plain variable (like `count`), the reactivity system cannot track this dependency because plain variables are not reactive sources.
+
+2. **Effects Only Re-run When Dependencies Change**: The effect scheduling mechanism only marks effects as "dirty" when their tracked dependencies (signals/sources) change.
+
+3. **flushSync Only Processes Dirty Effects**: The `flushSync` function only executes effects that are marked as dirty. Effects reading plain variables are never marked dirty when those variables change.
+
+## Example That Demonstrates the Issue
+```javascript
+let count = 0; // Plain variable - problematic!
+
+const destroy = effect_root(() => {
+  $effect(() => {
+    log.push(count); // Effect reads plain variable
+  });
+});
+
+// This works - effect runs once
+flushSync();
+
+// This DOESN'T work - effect doesn't re-run
+count = 1;
+flushSync();
+```
+
+## Expected Fix
+The issue is in how effects are scheduled when they depend on plain variables. The fix should ensure that:
+
+1. Effects that read plain variables are properly notified/scheduled when those variables change
+2. OR The documentation should clarify that only reactive sources ($state, signals) work with flushSync
+
+## Current Behavior
+- ✅ Effects run initially when created
+- ✅ Effects re-run when reactive sources change ($state, signals)
+- ❌ Effects do NOT re-run when plain variables change
+
+## Potential Fixes
+1. **Detect plain variable reads**: Make the effect scheduler aware of plain variable dependencies
+2. **Always mark effects as dirty**: Make effects re-run on every flushSync, regardless of dependencies
+3. **Documentation update**: Clarify that only reactive sources work with flushSync
+
+## Implementation Details
+The issue likely stems from the batch processing logic in `/packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/batch.js`. The `flushSync` function only processes effects that are in the `queued_root_effects` array, and effects only get queued when their dependencies change.

+// Trace the exact issue by examining the effect scheduling mechanism
+import { effect_root, user_effect } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/effects.js';
+import { flushSync } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/batch.js';
+import { queued_root_effects, schedule_effect } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/batch.js';
+
+console.log('Tracing the effect scheduling issue...');
+
+let log = [];
+let count = 0;
+
+const destroy = effect_root(() => {
+  // Create a user effect that reads the plain variable 'count'
+  const effect = user_effect(() => {
+    log.push(count);
+    console.log('Effect ran, count:', count);
+  });
+  
+  // Store the effect reference for inspection
+  globalThis.currentEffect = effect;
+});
+
+try {
+  // Initial flushSync
+  console.log('\n=== Initial flushSync ===');
+  console.log('queued_root_effects before flushSync:', queued_root_effects.length);
+  flushSync();
+  console.log('queued_root_effects after flushSync:', queued_root_effects.length);
+  console.log('Log after first flushSync:', log);
+  
+  // Update count
+  console.log('\n=== Updating count to 1 ===');
+  count = 1;
+  
+  // Manually schedule the effect to see if it works
+  console.log('Manually scheduling effect...');
+  schedule_effect(globalThis.currentEffect);
+  console.log('queued_root_effects after manual schedule:', queued_root_effects.length);
+  
+  // Second flushSync
+  console.log('\n=== Second flushSync ===');
+  flushSync();
+  console.log('queued_root_effects after second flushSync:', queued_root_effects.length);
+  console.log('Log after second flushSync:', log);
+  
+  // Check results
+  if (log.length === 1) {
+    console.error('\n❌ CONFIRMED: Effect did not re-run after count change');
+    console.error('The issue is that effects reading plain variables dont get rescheduled');
+  } else if (log.length === 2 && log[1] === 1) {
+    console.log('\n✅ Manual scheduling worked');
+  }

+// Understand the root cause by examining how effects detect changes
+import { effect_root, user_effect } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/effects.js';
+import { flushSync } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/batch.js';
+
+console.log('Understanding the root cause of the flushSync issue...');
+
+let log = [];
+let count = 0; // Plain variable - this is the issue!
+
+const destroy = effect_root(() => {
+  // Create user effect that reads a plain variable
+  user_effect(() => {
+    log.push(count);
+    console.log('Effect ran, count:', count);
+    
+    // The effect ran, but since 'count' is a plain variable
+    // there's no way for the reactivity system to know it was read
+    // and therefore no way to know when it changes
+  });
+});
+
+try {
+  // Initial flushSync
+  console.log('=== Initial flushSync ===');
+  flushSync();
+  console.log('Log:', log);
+  
+  // The problem: plain variables don't trigger reactivity
+  console.log('\n=== The Issue ===');
+  console.log('Plain variables like `count = 1` dont create dependencies');
+  console.log('When count changes, the effect has no way to know it needs to re-run');
+  console.log('The effect only knows about signals/sources it explicitly reads');
+  
+  // Update plain variable
+  count = 1;
+  
+  console.log('=== Second flushSync (after plain variable change) ===');
+  flushSync();
+  console.log('Log:', log);
+  
+  console.log('\n=== Analysis ===');
+  console.log('The effect didnt re-run because:');
+  console.log('1. Plain variables dont create reactive dependencies');
+  console.log('2. flushSync only processes effects that are scheduled/dirty');
+  console.log('3. Effects only become dirty when their dependencies signal changes');
+  console.log('4. Since count is a plain variable, the effect has no dependencies to monitor');
+  
+} finally {
+  destroy();
